</table>
<p><b>San Diego County</b> is a <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">county</a> located in the southwestern corner of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. As of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a>, the population was 3,095,313.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-QF-5">[5]</a></sup> making it the second-most populous county in California and the <a href="/wiki/County_statistics_of_the_United_States" title="County statistics of the United States">fifth-most populous</a> in the United States. Its <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> is <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR6_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR6-6">[6]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">eighth-most populous</a> city in the United States. It is the south-westernmost county in the 48 <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a>.</p>
<p>San Diego County comprises the <b>San Diego-Carlsbad Metropolitan Statistical Area</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OMB_13-01_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-OMB_13-01-7">[7]</a></sup> The San Diego-Carlsbad, CA Metropolitan Statistical Area is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Metropolitan Statistical Areas">17th most populous</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">metropolitan statistical area</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_primary_statistical_areas" title="List of United States primary statistical areas">18th most populous</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_primary_statistical_area" title="United States primary statistical area">primary statistical area</a> of the United States as of July 1, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCBSA_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstCBSA-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCSA_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstCSA-9">[9]</a></sup> San Diego is also part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego%E2%80%93Tijuana_metropolitan_area" title="San Diego–Tijuana metropolitan area">San Diego–Tijuana metropolitan area</a>, the largest metropolitan area shared between the United States and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>. Greater San Diego ranks as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_the_Americas_by_population" title="List of metropolitan areas in the Americas by population">38th largest metropolitan area in the Americas</a>.</p>
<p>San Diego County has 70 miles (110 km) of coastline. Most of the county has a mild <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semiarid_climate" title="Semiarid climate">semiarid climate</a>, though there are mountains that receive frost and snow in the wintertime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are also 16 naval and military installations of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Marine_Corps" title="U.S. Marine Corps">U.S. Marine Corps</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Coast_Guard" title="U.S. Coast Guard">U.S. Coast Guard</a> in San Diego County. These include the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Base_San_Diego" title="Naval Base San Diego">Naval Base San Diego</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Camp_Pendleton" title="Marine Corps Base Camp Pendleton">Marine Corps Base Camp Pendleton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Air_Station_Miramar" title="Marine Corps Air Station Miramar">Marine Corps Air Station Miramar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_North_Island" title="Naval Air Station North Island">Naval Air Station North Island</a>.</p>
<p>From north to south, San Diego County extends from the southern borders of <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverside_County" title="Riverside County">Riverside County</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Mexico–United States border">Mexico–United States border</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a>. From west to east, San Diego County stretches from the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> to its boundary with <a href="/wiki/Imperial_County,_California" title="Imperial County, California">Imperial County</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_San_Diego" title="History of San Diego">History of San Diego</a></div>
<p>The area which is now San Diego County has been inhabited for more than 10,000 years by <a href="/wiki/Kumeyaay" title="Kumeyaay">Kumeyaay</a> (also called Diegueño), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luise%C3%B1o_people" title="Luiseño people">Luiseño</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cupe%C3%B1o_people" title="Cupeño people">Cupeño</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cahuilla_people" title="Cahuilla people">Cahuilla</a> Indians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1542, the Portuguese-born explorer <a href="/wiki/Juan_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Cabrillo" title="Juan Rodríguez Cabrillo">Juan Rodríguez Cabrillo</a>, sailing for Spain, claimed <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Bay" title="San Diego Bay">San Diego Bay</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>, and he named the site <i>San Miguel</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> In November 1602, <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Vizca%C3%ADno" title="Sebastián Vizcaíno">Sebastián Vizcaíno</a> surveyed the harbor and what are now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_Bay,_San_Diego,_California" title="Mission Bay, San Diego, California">Mission Bay</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Point_Loma" title="Point Loma">Point Loma</a> and named the area for <a href="/wiki/Didacus_of_Alcal%C3%A1" title="Didacus of Alcalá">Saint Didacus</a>, a Spaniard more commonly known as <i>San Diego</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> European settlement in what is now San Diego County began with the founding of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_Presidio" title="San Diego Presidio">San Diego Presidio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcal%C3%A1" title="Mission San Diego de Alcalá">Mission San Diego de Alcalá</a> by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> soldiers and clerics in 1769.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> This county was part of <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a> under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">Viceroyalty of New Spain</a> until the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_declaration_of_independence" title="Mexican declaration of independence">Mexican declaration of independence</a>. From 1821 through 1848 this area was part of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.</p>
<p>San Diego County became part of the United States as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo</a> in 1848, ending the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S.-Mexican_War" title="U.S.-Mexican War">U.S.-Mexican War</a>. This treaty designated the new border as terminating at a point on the Pacific Ocean coast which would result in the border passing one Spanish league south of the southernmost portion of <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Bay" title="San Diego Bay">San Diego Bay</a>, thus ensuring that the United States received all of this natural harbor.</p>
<p>San Diego County was one of the original counties of California, and it was created at the time of California statehood in 1850.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coy_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-coy-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:221</sup></p>
<p>At the time of its establishment in 1850, San Diego County was relatively large, and included all of southernmost California which was south and east of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County" title="Los Angeles County">Los Angeles County</a>. As such it included areas of what are now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inyo_County" title="Inyo County">Inyo County</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Bernardino_County" title="San Bernardino County">San Bernardino County</a>, as well as all of what is now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverside_County" title="Riverside County">Riverside County</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_County,_California" title="Imperial County, California">Imperial County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coy_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-coy-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:221</sup></p>
<p>During the later part of the 19th century, there were numerous changes in the boundaries of San Diego County, when various areas became separated for the counties mentioned above. The most recent changes were the establishments of Riverside County in 1893<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coy_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-coy-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:207</sup> and Imperial County in 1907.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coy_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-coy-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:113</sup> Imperial County was also the last county to be established in California, and after this division, San Diego no longer extended from the Pacific Ocean to the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado River</a>, and it no longer covered the entire border between California and Mexico.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Diego-Tijuana_JPLLandsat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="724" data-file-width="1150" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/San_Diego-Tijuana_JPLLandsat.jpg/220px-San_Diego-Tijuana_JPLLandsat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/San_Diego-Tijuana_JPLLandsat.jpg/330px-San_Diego-Tijuana_JPLLandsat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/San_Diego-Tijuana_JPLLandsat.jpg/440px-San_Diego-Tijuana_JPLLandsat.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Diego-Tijuana_JPLLandsat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Many of the cities seen from the sky as part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego-Tijuana_metropolitan_area" title="San Diego-Tijuana metropolitan area">San Diego-Tijuana metropolitan area</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">U.S. Census Bureau</a>, the county has a total area of 4,526 square miles (11,720 km<sup>2</sup>), of which 4,207 square miles (10,900 km<sup>2</sup>) is land and 319 square miles (830 km<sup>2</sup>) (7.0%) is water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR1_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR1-16">[16]</a></sup> The county is larger in area than the combined states of Rhode Island and Delaware.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>San Diego County has a varied topography. On its western side is 70 miles (110 km) of coastline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Most of San Diego between the coast and the <a href="/wiki/Laguna_Mountains" title="Laguna Mountains">Laguna Mountains</a> consists of hills, <a href="/wiki/Mesa" title="Mesa">mesas</a>, and small <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">canyons</a>. Snow-capped (in winter) mountains rise to the northeast, with the <a href="/wiki/Sonoran_Desert" title="Sonoran Desert">Sonoran Desert</a> to the far east. <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_National_Forest" title="Cleveland National Forest">Cleveland National Forest</a> is spread across the central portion of the county, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anza-Borrego_Desert" title="Anza-Borrego Desert">Anza-Borrego Desert State Park</a> occupies most of the northeast.</p>
<p>Although the western third of the county is primarily urban, the mountains and deserts in the eastern two-thirds of the county consist primarily of undeveloped <a href="/wiki/Backcountry" title="Backcountry">backcountry</a>. Most of these backcountry areas are home to a native plant community known as <a href="/wiki/Chaparral" title="Chaparral">chaparral</a>. San Diego County contains more than a million acres (4,000 km²) of chaparral, twice as much as any other California county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>North San Diego County is known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_County,_San_Diego" title="North County, San Diego">North County</a>; the exact geographic definitions of "North County" vary, but it includes the northern suburbs and sometimes certain northern neighborhoods of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_of_San_Diego" title="City of San Diego">City of San Diego</a>.</p>
<p>The eastern suburbs are collectively known as <a href="/wiki/East_County,_San_Diego" title="East County, San Diego">East County</a>, though most still lie in the western third of the county. The southern suburbs and southern detached portion of the city of San Diego, extending to the Mexican border, are collectively referred to as <a href="/wiki/South_Bay,_San_Diego" title="South Bay, San Diego">South Bay</a>.</p>
<p>Periodically the area has been subject to <a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">wildfires</a> that force thousands to evacuate. The most recent are the <a href="/wiki/May_2014_San_Diego_County_wildfires" title="May 2014 San Diego County wildfires">May 2014 San Diego County wildfires</a>; before them was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Witch_Creek_Fire" title="Witch Creek Fire">Witch Creek Fire</a> in 2007 and the <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Fire_(2003)" title="Cedar Fire (2003)">Cedar Fire</a> in 2003. California defines a fire season in which fires are most likely to occur, usually between the months of late July and late October (which are the driest months of the area). Signs are posted in numerous spots of the county providing information on the level of threats from fires based on weather conditions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_San_Diego,_California" title="Climate of San Diego, California">Climate of San Diego, California</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mountlagunasmall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="480" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Mountlagunasmall.jpg/220px-Mountlagunasmall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Mountlagunasmall.jpg/330px-Mountlagunasmall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Mountlagunasmall.jpg/440px-Mountlagunasmall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mountlagunasmall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cleveland_National_Forest" title="Cleveland National Forest">Cleveland National Forest</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> system, the San Diego area straddles areas of <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (CSa) to the north and <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a> (BSh) to the south and east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> As a result, it is often described as "arid Mediterranean" and "semi-arid steppe". San Diego's climate is characterized by warm, dry summers and mild winters with most of the annual precipitation falling between November and March. The city has mild, mostly dry weather, with an average of 201 days above 70 °F (21 °C) and low rainfall (9–13 inches (23–33 cm) annually). Summer temperatures are generally warm, with average highs of 70–78 °F (21–26 °C) and lows of 55–66 °F (13–19 °C). Temperatures exceed 90 °F (32 °C) only four days a year. Most rainfall occurs from November to April. Winter temperatures are mild, with average high temperatures of 66–70 °F (19–21 °C) and lows of 50–56 °F (10–13 °C).</p>
<p>The climate in the San Diego area, like much of California, often varies significantly over short geographical distances resulting in <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimates</a>. In San Diego's case this is mainly due to the city's topography (the Bay, and the numerous hills, mountains, and canyons). Frequently, particularly during the "May gray/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/June_gloom" title="June gloom">June gloom</a>" period, a thick <a href="/wiki/Marine_layer" title="Marine layer">marine layer</a> will keep the air cool and damp within a few miles of the coast, but will yield to bright cloudless sunshine approximately 5–10 miles (8.0–16.1 km) inland. This happens every year in May and June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Even in the absence of June gloom, inland areas tend to experience much more significant temperature variations than coastal areas, where the ocean serves as a moderating influence. Thus, for example, downtown San Diego averages January lows of 50 °F (10 °C) and August highs of 78 °F (26 °C). The city of El Cajon, just 10 miles (16 km) northeast of downtown San Diego, averages January lows of 42 °F (6 °C) and August highs of 88 °F (31 °C).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weather1_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-weather1-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weather_el_cajon_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-weather_el_cajon-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rainfall along the coast averages about 10 inches (25 cm) of precipitation annually, which occurs mainly during the cooler months of December through April. Though there are few wet days per month during the rainy period, rainfall can be heavy when it does occur. However, the rainfall is greater in the higher elevations of San Diego. Some of the higher areas of San Diego can receive 11–13 inches (28–33 cm) of rain a year.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_protected_areas">National protected areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: National protected areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cabrillo_National_Monument" title="Cabrillo National Monument">Cabrillo National Monument</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cleveland_National_Forest" title="Cleveland National Forest">Cleveland National Forest</a> (part)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/San_Diego_National_Wildlife_Refuge_Complex" title="San Diego National Wildlife Refuge Complex">San Diego National Wildlife Refuge Complex</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> which includes
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/San_Diego_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="San Diego National Wildlife Refuge">San Diego National Wildlife Refuge</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Bay_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="San Diego Bay National Wildlife Refuge">San Diego Bay National Wildlife Refuge</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tijuana_Slough_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Tijuana Slough National Wildlife Refuge">Tijuana Slough National Wildlife Refuge</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seal_Beach_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Seal Beach National Wildlife Refuge">Seal Beach National Wildlife Refuge</a> (located in <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>There are 7 official <a href="/wiki/Wilderness_area" title="Wilderness area">wilderness areas</a> in San Diego County that are part of the <a href="/wiki/National_Wilderness_Preservation_System" title="National Wilderness Preservation System">National Wilderness Preservation System</a>. Four of these are integral parts of Cleveland National Forest, whereas three are managed by the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Land_Management" title="Bureau of Land Management">Bureau of Land Management</a>. Some of these extend into neighboring counties (as indicated below):</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Otay_Mountain_Wilderness" title="Otay Mountain Wilderness">Otay Mountain Wilderness</a> (BLM)</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pine_Creek_Wilderness&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pine Creek Wilderness (page does not exist)">Pine Creek Wilderness</a> (Cleveland National Forest)</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hauser_Wilderness&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hauser Wilderness (page does not exist)">Hauser Wilderness</a> (Cleveland National Forest)</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Carrizo_Gorge_Wilderness&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Carrizo Gorge Wilderness (page does not exist)">Carrizo Gorge Wilderness</a> (BLM)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sawtooth_Mountains_Wilderness" title="Sawtooth Mountains Wilderness">Sawtooth Mountains Wilderness</a> (BLM)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Agua_Tibia_Wilderness" title="Agua Tibia Wilderness">Agua Tibia Wilderness</a> (Cleveland National Forest) partly in Riverside County</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=San_Mateo_Canyon_Wilderness&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="San Mateo Canyon Wilderness (page does not exist)">San Mateo Canyon Wilderness</a> (Cleveland National Forest) mostly in Riverside County</li>
</ul>

<p>There are 236 mountain summits and peaks in San Diego County<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> including:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>

<li><a href="/wiki/Cuyamaca_Peak" title="Cuyamaca Peak">Cuyamaca Peak</a> (second highest point in San Diego County)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cowles_Mountain" title="Cowles Mountain">Cowles Mountain</a> (highest point in the city of San Diego)</li>
<li>Mount Helix</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hot_Springs_Mountain" title="Hot Springs Mountain">Hot Springs Mountain</a> (highest point in San Diego County)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Margarita_Peak" title="Margarita Peak">Margarita Peak</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Soledad" title="Mount Soledad">Mount Soledad</a></li>
<li>Stonewall Mountain</li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_San_Diego_County" title="Demographics of San Diego County">Demographics of San Diego County</a></div>
<p>Half of the county's population lives in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chula_Vista,_California" title="Chula Vista, California">Chula Vista</a>. In 2000, only about 3% of San Diego County residents left the county for work while 40,000 people commuted into the metropolitan area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Race">Race</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Race">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Filipino_Americans#San_Diego_County" title="Demographics of Filipino Americans">Demographics of Filipino Americans § San Diego County</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a> reported that San Diego County had a population of 3,095,313. The racial makeup of San Diego County was 1,981,442 (64.0%) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">White</a>, 158,213 (5.1%) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">African American</a>, 26,340 (0.9%) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">Native American</a>, 336,091 (10.9%) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">Asian</a> (4.7% Filipino, 1.6% Chinese, 1.4% Vietnamese, 3.2% Other Asian), 15,337 (0.5%) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">Pacific Islander</a>, 419,465 (13.6%) from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">other races</a>, and 158,425 (5.0%) from two or more races. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race were 991,348 persons (32.0%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2009, the racial makeup of the county was 79.4% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">White American</a>, 5.6% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Black</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">African American</a>, 1% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Native American</a>, 10.4% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Asian</a>, 0.5% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Pacific Islander</a>, 10.3% from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">other races</a>, and 3.6% from two or more races. 31.3% of the population were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Latino</a> of any race.</p>
<p>67.0% spoke only English at home; 21.9% spoke Spanish, 3.1% <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a> and 1.2% <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_demographics">Other demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2009 Census Bureau estimates, there were 3,053,793 people, 1,067,846 households, and 663,449 families residing in the county. The population density was 670 people per square mile (259/km²). There were 1,142,245 housing units at an average density of 248 per square mile (96/km²).</p>
<p>In 2000 there were 994,677 households out of which 33.9% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 50.7% were married couples living together, 11.6% had a female householder with no husband present, and 33.3% were non-families. 24.2% of all households were made up of individuals and 7.9% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.73 and the average family size was 3.29.</p>
<p>As of 2000, in the county the population was spread out with 25.7% under the age of 18, 11.30% from 18 to 24, 32.0% from 25 to 44, 19.8% from 45 to 64, and 11.2% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 33 years. For every 100 females there were 101.2 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 99.7 males.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Income">Income</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Income">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the 2000 Census, the median income for a household in the county was $47,067, and the median income for a family was $53,438. Males had a median income of $36,952 versus $30,356 for females. The per capita income for the county was $22,926. About 8.9% of families and 12.4% of the population were below the poverty line, including 16.5% of those under age 18 and 6.8% of those age 65 or over.</p>
<p>Much of the county's high-income residents are concentrated in the northern part of the city of San Diego. The San Diego metropolitan area has two places with both a population of over 50,000 and a per capita income of over $40,000: <a href="/wiki/Carlsbad,_California" title="Carlsbad, California">Carlsbad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Encinitas,_California" title="Encinitas, California">Encinitas</a>.</p>
<p>The county's largest continuous high-income urban area is a triangle from a first point on the northern edge of Carlsbad, a second point southeast of <a href="/wiki/Escondido,_California" title="Escondido, California">Escondido</a>, and a third point on the southern edge of <a href="/wiki/La_Jolla" title="La Jolla">La Jolla</a>. It contains all or most of the cities of Carlsbad, Encinitas, <a href="/wiki/Solana_Beach,_California" title="Solana Beach, California">Solana Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Del_Mar,_California" title="Del Mar, California">Del Mar</a>, and Poway in addition to a substantial portion of northern San Diego.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US-CB-B01003-B19025_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-US-CB-B01003-B19025-48">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Diego_City_and_County_Administration_Building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2540" data-file-width="3316" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/San_Diego_City_and_County_Administration_Building.jpg/220px-San_Diego_City_and_County_Administration_Building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/San_Diego_City_and_County_Administration_Building.jpg/330px-San_Diego_City_and_County_Administration_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/San_Diego_City_and_County_Administration_Building.jpg/440px-San_Diego_City_and_County_Administration_Building.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Diego_City_and_County_Administration_Building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/San_Diego_County_Administration_Center" title="San Diego County Administration Center">San Diego County Administration Center</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_San_Diego_County,_California" title="Government of San Diego County, California">Government of San Diego County, California</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_San_Diego_County,_California" title="Government of San Diego County, California">Government of San Diego County</a> is defined and authorized under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_Constitution" title="California Constitution">California Constitution</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_law" title="California law">California law</a>, and the Charter of the County of San Diego.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> Much of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_California" title="Government of California">Government of California</a> is in practice the responsibility of county governments such as the Government of San Diego County. The County government provides countywide services such as elections and voter registration, law enforcement, jails, vital records, property records, tax collection, public health, and social services. In addition the County serves as the local government for all unincorporated areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> Some chartered cities such as <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chula_Vista,_California" title="Chula Vista, California">Chula Vista</a> provide municipal services such as police, public safety, libraries, parks and recreation, and zoning. Other cities such as <a href="/wiki/Del_Mar,_California" title="Del Mar, California">Del Mar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vista,_California" title="Vista, California">Vista</a> arrange to have the County provide some or all of these services on a contract basis.</p>
<p>The county government is composed of the elected five-member <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_County_Board_of_Supervisors" title="San Diego County Board of Supervisors">Board of Supervisors</a>, several other elected offices and officers including the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_County_Sheriff%27s_Department" title="San Diego County Sheriff's Department">Sheriff</a>, the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_County_District_Attorney" title="San Diego County District Attorney">District Attorney</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County_Assessor/Recorder/County_Clerk&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="San Diego County Assessor/Recorder/County Clerk (page does not exist)">Assessor/Recorder/County Clerk</a>, and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County_Treasurer/Tax_Collector&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="San Diego County Treasurer/Tax Collector (page does not exist)">Treasurer/Tax Collector</a>, and numerous county departments and entities under the supervision of the Chief Administrative Officer such as the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_County,_California_Probation" title="San Diego County, California Probation">Probation Department</a>. In addition, several entities of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_California" title="Government of California">government of California</a> have jurisdiction conterminous with San Diego County, such as the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Superior_Court_of_San_Diego_County&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Superior Court of San Diego County (page does not exist)">San Diego Superior Court</a>.</p>
<p>Under its foundational Charter, the five-member elected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_County_Board_of_Supervisors" title="San Diego County Board of Supervisors">San Diego County Board of Supervisors</a> is the county legislature. The board operates in a legislative, executive, and <a href="/wiki/Quasi-judicial_body" title="Quasi-judicial body">quasi-judicial</a> capacity. As a legislative authority, it can pass ordinances for the unincorporated areas (ordinances that affect the whole county, like posting of restaurant ratings, must be ratified by the individual city). As an executive body, it can tell the county departments what to do, and how to do it. As a quasi-judicial body, the Board is the final venue of appeal in the local planning process.</p>
<p>As of January 2013 the members of the San Diego County Board of Supervisors are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Greg Cox, District 1, Chairman</li>
<li>Dianne Jacob, District 2</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dave_Roberts_(California_politician)" title="Dave Roberts (California politician)">Dave Roberts</a>, District 3</li>
<li>Ron Roberts, District 4 (no relation to Dave Roberts)</li>
<li>Bill Horn, District 5</li>
</ul>
<p>For several decades, ending in 2013, all five supervisors were <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">white</a>, graduates of <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_State_University" title="San Diego State University">San Diego State University</a>, and had been in office since 1995 or earlier. The Board was criticized for this homogeneity, which was made possible because supervisors draw their own district lines and are not subject to term limits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> (In 2010 voters put term limits in place, but they only apply going forward, so that each incumbent supervisor can serve an additional two terms before being termed out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup>) That pattern was broken in 2013 when Slater-Price retired; she was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a> Dave Roberts, who won election to the seat in November 2012 and was inaugurated in January 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>The San Diego County Code is the <a href="/wiki/Codification_(law)" title="Codification (law)">codified</a> law of San Diego County in the form of <a href="/wiki/Local_ordinance" title="Local ordinance">ordinances</a> passed by the Board of Supervisors. The Administrative Code establishes the powers and duties of all officers and the procedures and rules of operation of all departments.</p>
<p>The county motto is "The noblest motive is the public good." County government offices are housed in the historic <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_County_Administration_Center" title="San Diego County Administration Center">County Administration Center</a> Building, constructed in 1935-1938 with funding from the <a href="/wiki/Works_Progress_Administration" title="Works Progress Administration">Works Progress Administration</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup></p>

<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_San_Diego_County" title="Politics of San Diego County">Politics of San Diego County</a></div>
<p>As of June 2013, there are 1,556,739 registered voters in San Diego County. Of those, 547,897 (35.2%) are registered Democratic, 526,306 (33.8%) are registered Republican, 401,340 (25.8%) declined to state a political party, 51,993 (3.3%) are registered American Independence Party, 11,657 (0.7%) are registered Libertarian, 7,675 (0.5%) are registered Green, and 4,012 (0.3%) are registered Peace &amp; Freedom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup></p>

<p>San Diego County has historically been a <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> stronghold. The Republican presidential nominee carried the county in every presidential election from 1948 through 2004, except in 1992 when <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> won a plurality. In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> became the first <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> presidential candidate to win a majority of votes in San Diego County since World War II; he won a majority of county votes again in 2012.</p>
<p>The city of San Diego itself is more Democratic than the county's average and has voted for Democrats in each presidential election since 1992. Various cities within the county are swing areas that have split their votes in elections since 2000. Republican strength is concentrated in North County, as well as the inland portions.</p>
<p>One unique feature of the political scene is the use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Hall_(sports_venue)" title="Golden Hall (sports venue)">Golden Hall</a>, a convention facility next to San Diego's City Hall, as "Election Central." The County Registrar of Voters rents the hall to distribute election results. Supporters and political observers gather to watch the results come in; supporters of the various candidates parade around the hall, carrying signs and chanting; candidates give their victory and concession speeches and host parties for campaign volunteers and donors at the site; and television stations broadcast live from the floor of the convention center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup> The atmosphere at Election Central on the evening of election day has been compared to the voting portion of a political party national convention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>On Nov 4, 2008 San Diego County voted 53.8% for Proposition 8 which amended the California Constitution to ban same-sex marriages, thus restoring <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_22_(2000)" title="California Proposition 22 (2000)">Proposition 22</a> which was overturned by a ruling from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_Supreme_Court" title="California Supreme Court">California Supreme Court</a>. However the city of San Diego, along with Del Mar, Encinitas, and Solana Beach, voted against Proposition 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_and_state_representation">Federal and state representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Federal and state representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">U.S. House of Representatives</a>, San Diego County is split between five congressional districts:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_49th_congressional_district" title="California's 49th congressional district">California's 49th congressional district</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Darrell_Issa" title="Darrell Issa">Darrell Issa</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_50th_congressional_district" title="California's 50th congressional district">California's 50th congressional district</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Duncan_D._Hunter" title="Duncan D. Hunter">Duncan D. Hunter</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_51st_congressional_district" title="California's 51st congressional district">California's 51st congressional district</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Juan_Vargas" title="Juan Vargas">Juan Vargas</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_52nd_congressional_district" title="California's 52nd congressional district">California's 52nd congressional district</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Scott_Peters_(politician)" title="Scott Peters (politician)">Scott Peters</a> and</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_53rd_congressional_district" title="California's 53rd congressional district">California's 53rd congressional district</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Susan_Davis_(politician)" title="Susan Davis (politician)">Susan Davis</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Assembly" title="California State Assembly">California State Assembly</a>, San Diego County is split between seven legislative districts:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_71st_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 71st State Assembly district">the 71st Assembly District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Randy_Voepel" title="Randy Voepel">Randy Voepel</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_75th_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 75th State Assembly district">the 75th Assembly District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Marie_Waldron" title="Marie Waldron">Marie Waldron</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_76th_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 76th State Assembly district">the 76th Assembly District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Rocky Chávez">Rocky Chávez</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_77th_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 77th State Assembly district">the 77th Assembly District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Brian_Maienschein" title="Brian Maienschein">Brian Maienschein</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_78th_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 78th State Assembly district">the 78th Assembly District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Democratic_Party" title="California Democratic Party">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Todd_Gloria" title="Todd Gloria">Todd Gloria</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_79th_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 79th State Assembly district">the 79th Assembly District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Democratic_Party" title="California Democratic Party">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Weber" title="Shirley Weber">Shirley Weber</a>, and</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_80th_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 80th State Assembly district">the 80th Assembly District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Democratic_Party" title="California Democratic Party">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Lorena_Gonzalez_Fletcher" title="Lorena Gonzalez Fletcher">Lorena Gonzalez Fletcher</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Senate" title="California State Senate">California State Senate</a>, San Diego County is split between four legislative districts:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_36th_State_Senate_district" title="California's 36th State Senate district">the 36th Senate District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Bates" title="Patricia Bates">Patricia Bates</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_38th_State_Senate_district" title="California's 38th State Senate district">the 38th Senate District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Joel_Anderson" title="Joel Anderson">Joel Anderson</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_39th_State_Senate_district" title="California's 39th State Senate district">the 39th Senate District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Democratic_Party" title="California Democratic Party">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Toni_Atkins" title="Toni Atkins">Toni Atkins</a>, and</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California%27s_40th_State_Senate_district" title="California's 40th State Senate district">the 40th Senate District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Democratic_Party" title="California Democratic Party">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Ben_Hueso" title="Ben Hueso">Ben Hueso</a>.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Beer_in_San_Diego_County,_California" title="Beer in San Diego County, California">Beer in San Diego County, California</a></div>
<p>Arising from an effort by the state government to identify regional economies, San Diego County and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_County,_California" title="Imperial County, California">Imperial County</a> are part of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Border_Region_(California)" title="Southern Border Region (California)">Southern Border Region</a>, one of nine such regions. As a regional economy, the Southern Border Region is the smallest but most economically diverse region in the state. However, the two counties maintain weak relations and have little in common aside from their common border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>San Diego County's <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> industry was worth $1.85 billion in 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[65]</a></sup> and is one of the top five egg producing counties in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[66]</a></sup> In 2013, San Diego County also had the most <a href="/wiki/Small_farm#United_States" title="Small farm">small farms</a> of any county in the United States, and had the 19th largest agricultural economy of any county in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[67]</a></sup> According to the San Diego Farm Bureau, San Diego County is the United States leading producer of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avocados" title="Avocados">avocados</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Plant_nursery" title="Plant nursery">nursery crops</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Horton_Plaza.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="900" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Horton_Plaza.jpg/170px-Horton_Plaza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Horton_Plaza.jpg/255px-Horton_Plaza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Horton_Plaza.jpg/340px-Horton_Plaza.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Horton_Plaza.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Westfield_Horton_Plaza" title="Westfield Horton Plaza">Horton Plaza</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Tourism plays a large part in the economics of the San Diego metropolitan area. Tourists are drawn to the region for a well rounded experience, everything from shopping to surfing as well as its mild climate. Its numerous tourist destinations include <a href="/wiki/Westfield_Horton_Plaza" title="Westfield Horton Plaza">Horton Plaza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westfield_UTC" title="Westfield UTC">Westfield UTC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seaport_Village" title="Seaport Village">Seaport Village</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westfield_Mission_Valley" title="Westfield Mission Valley">Westfield Mission Valley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fashion_Valley_Mall" title="Fashion Valley Mall">Fashion Valley Mall</a> for shopping. <a href="/wiki/SeaWorld_San_Diego" title="SeaWorld San Diego">SeaWorld San Diego</a> and <a href="/wiki/Legoland_California" title="Legoland California">Legoland California</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amusement_parks" title="Amusement parks">amusement parks</a>. Golf courses such as <a href="/wiki/Torrey_Pines_Golf_Course" title="Torrey Pines Golf Course">Torrey Pines Golf Course</a> and Balboa Park Golf Course. Museums such as the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Museum_of_Man" title="San Diego Museum of Man">San Diego Museum of Man</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Museum_of_Art" title="San Diego Museum of Art">San Diego Museum of Art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reuben_H._Fleet_Science_Center" title="Reuben H. Fleet Science Center">Reuben H. Fleet Science Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Natural_History_Museum" title="San Diego Natural History Museum">San Diego Natural History Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Midway_Museum" title="USS Midway Museum">USS Midway Museum</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_Air_and_Space_Museum" title="San Diego Air and Space Museum">San Diego Air and Space Museum</a>. Historical places such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaslamp_Quarter" title="Gaslamp Quarter">Gaslamp Quarter</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balboa_Park,_San_Diego,_California" title="Balboa Park, San Diego, California">Balboa Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_San_Diego_State_Historic_Park" title="Old Town San Diego State Historic Park">Old Town San Diego State Historic Park</a>. Wildlife refuges, zoos, and aquariums such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Birch_Aquarium_at_Scripps" title="Birch Aquarium at Scripps">Birch Aquarium at Scripps</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_Zoo%27s_Safari_Park" title="San Diego Zoo's Safari Park">San Diego Zoo's Safari Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Zoo" title="San Diego Zoo">San Diego Zoo</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Diego-La_Jolla_Underwater_Park" title="San Diego-La Jolla Underwater Park">San Diego-La Jolla Underwater Park</a>. Outdoor destinations include the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Ranges" title="Peninsular Ranges">Peninsular Ranges</a> for <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">hiking</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biking" title="Biking">biking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountainboarding" title="Mountainboarding">mountainboarding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trail_riding" title="Trail riding">trail riding</a>. <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">Surfing</a> locations include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swami%27s_(surfing)" title="Swami's (surfing)">Swami's</a>, Stone Steps Beach, <a href="/wiki/Torrey_Pines_State_Beach" title="Torrey Pines State Beach">Torrey Pines State Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_State_Beach" title="Cardiff State Beach">Cardiff State Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Onofre_State_Beach" title="San Onofre State Beach">San Onofre State Beach</a> and the southern portion of <a href="/wiki/Black%27s_Beach" title="Black's Beach">Black's Beach</a>.</p>
<p>The region is host to the second largest cruise ship industry in California which generates an estimated $2 million annually from purchases of food, fuel, supplies, and maintenance services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SDCruiseShips_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-SDCruiseShips-73">[69]</a></sup> In 2008 the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_San_Diego" title="Port of San Diego">Port of San Diego</a> hosted 252 ship calls and more than 800,000 passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>San Diego County contains three public state universities: <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Diego" title="University of California, San Diego">University of California, San Diego</a>; <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_State_University" title="San Diego State University">San Diego State University</a>; and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_State_University,_San_Marcos" title="California State University, San Marcos">California State University, San Marcos</a>. Major private universities in the county include <a href="/wiki/University_of_San_Diego" title="University of San Diego">University of San Diego</a> (USD), <a href="/wiki/Point_Loma_Nazarene_University" title="Point Loma Nazarene University">Point Loma Nazarene University</a> (PLNU), <a href="/wiki/Alliant_International_University" title="Alliant International University">Alliant International University</a> (AIU), and <a href="/wiki/National_University_(California)" title="National University (California)">National University</a>.</p>
<p>Within the county there are 24 public elementary school districts, 6 high school districts, and 12 unified school districts. There are also 5 community college districts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are two separate public library systems in San Diego County: the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Public_Library" title="San Diego Public Library">San Diego Public Library</a> serving the city of San Diego, and the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_County_Library" title="San Diego County Library">San Diego County Library</a> serving all other areas of the county. In 2010 the county library had 33 branches and two bookmobiles; circulated over 10.7 million books, CDs, DVDs, and other material formats; recorded 5.7 million visits to library branches; and hosted 21,132 free programs and events. The San Diego County Library is one of the 25 busiest libraries in the nation as measured by materials circulated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Decatur_(DDG-73).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1575" data-file-width="2100" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/USS_Decatur_%28DDG-73%29.jpg/220px-USS_Decatur_%28DDG-73%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/USS_Decatur_%28DDG-73%29.jpg/330px-USS_Decatur_%28DDG-73%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/USS_Decatur_%28DDG-73%29.jpg/440px-USS_Decatur_%28DDG-73%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Decatur_(DDG-73).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Decatur_(DDG-73)" title="USS Decatur (DDG-73)">USS Decatur (DDG-73)</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a> is the headquarters of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a>'s Eleventh Naval District and is the Navy's principal location for West Coast and Pacific Ocean operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Naval_Base_San_Diego" title="Naval Base San Diego">Naval Base San Diego</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> is principal home to the Pacific Fleet (although the <a href="/wiki/Headquarters" title="Headquarters">headquarters</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAS_North_Island" title="NAS North Island">NAS North Island</a> is located on the north side of <a href="/wiki/Coronado,_California" title="Coronado, California">Coronado</a>, and is home to Headquarters for Naval Air Forces and Naval Air Force Pacific, the bulk of the Pacific Fleet's helicopter squadrons, and part of the West Coast <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a> fleet.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Naval_Special_Warfare_Center" title="Naval Special Warfare Center">Naval Special Warfare Center</a> is the primary training center for <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_SEALs" title="United States Navy SEALs">SEALs</a>, and is also located on Coronado. The area contains five major naval bases and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Marines" title="U.S. Marines">U.S. Marines</a> base <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camp_Pendleton" title="Camp Pendleton">Camp Pendleton</a>. Marine Corps Base Camp Pendleton is the major <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">West Coast</a> base of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a> and serves as its prime amphibious training base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Estes_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Estes-79">[75]</a></sup> It is located on the <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a> coast, bordered by <a href="/wiki/Oceanside,_California" title="Oceanside, California">Oceanside</a> to the south, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Clemente" title="San Clemente">San Clemente</a> to the north, and <a href="/wiki/Fallbrook,_California" title="Fallbrook, California">Fallbrook</a> to the east.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._Navy">U.S. Navy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: U.S. Navy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_San_Diego" title="Culture of San Diego">Culture of San Diego</a></div>
<p>The culture of San Diego is influenced heavily by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Culture" title="American Culture">American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexican</a> <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultures</a> due to its position as a <a href="/wiki/Border_town" title="Border town">border town</a>, its large <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic</a> population, and its history as part of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">Spanish America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>. The area's longtime association with the U.S. military also contributes to its culture. Present-day culture includes many historical and tourist attractions, a thriving musical and theatrical scene, numerous notable special events, a varied cuisine, and a reputation as one of America's premier centers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Craft_brewery" title="Craft brewery">craft brewing</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_San_Diego" title="Sports in San Diego">Sports in San Diego</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sites_of_interest">Sites of interest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sites of interest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Laguna_Observatory" title="Mount Laguna Observatory">Mount Laguna Observatory</a>, owned and primarily operated by <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_State_University" title="San Diego State University">San Diego State University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Palomar_Observatory" title="Palomar Observatory">Palomar Observatory</a>, owned and primarily operated by the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">California Institute of Technology</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramona_Valley" title="Ramona Valley">Ramona Valley</a> wine-producing region, located 28 miles (45 km) northeast of the City of San Diego</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Zoo_Safari_Park" title="San Diego Zoo Safari Park">San Diego Zoo Safari Park</a>, formerly known as the San Diego Wild Animal Park, 35 miles (56 km) north of the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Zoo" title="San Diego Zoo">San Diego Zoo</a> and east of Escondido</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SeaWorld_San_Diego" title="SeaWorld San Diego">Sea World</a> of San Diego, on Mission Bay.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_Bay,_San_Diego,_California" title="Mission Bay, San Diego, California">Mission Bay</a> Recreation Area, including Fiesta Island, a sheltered bay popular for water sports, also known for the annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Over_the_line" title="Over the line">Over the line</a> tournament.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcala" title="Mission San Diego de Alcala">Mission San Diego de Alcala</a>, the first of California's 21 Spanish missions. It is an operating Roman Catholic parish and also is open for historical interest tours during the week. It is located near the interchange of Interstates 8 and 15.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_San_Luis_Rey" title="Mission San Luis Rey">Mission San Luis Rey</a>, founded on June 13, 1798 by Padre Fermín Lasuén. It is the 18th of the Spanish missions established in California. It is an operating Roman Catholic parish and is open every day for historical interest tours. It is located near Route 76 in the Oceanside area.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balboa_Park,_San_Diego,_California" title="Balboa Park, San Diego, California">Balboa Park</a>, with numerous museums and other cultural locations, located just north of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_San_Diego" title="Downtown San Diego">Downtown San Diego</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Zoo" title="San Diego Zoo">San Diego Zoo</a>, located in Balboa Park</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Presidio_Park" title="Presidio Park">Presidio Park</a>, located on a bluff directly above Old Town, a city historic park on the site of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_Presidio" title="San Diego Presidio">San Diego Presidio</a>, the first European settlement in California.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Bay" title="San Diego Bay">San Diego Bay</a> contains the <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_Midway_(CV-41)" title="USS Midway (CV-41)">USS <i>Midway</i></a> now used as a memorial ship and as a floating museum, and the eight floating museum ships of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_Maritime_Museum" title="San Diego Maritime Museum">San Diego Maritime Museum</a>. Harbor cruises, sailing, and sport fishing are also available.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LEGOLAND_California" title="LEGOLAND California">LEGOLAND California</a> Resort is a "LEGO" themed resort in <a href="/wiki/Carlsbad,_California" title="Carlsbad, California">Carlsbad</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alta_Vista_Gardens" title="Alta Vista Gardens">Alta Vista Gardens</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Botanical_Garden" title="Botanical Garden">Botanical Garden</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vista,_California" title="Vista, California">Vista, California</a> dedicated to bringing together 'People, Nature &amp; Art'.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>San Diego County is served by many newspapers. The major regional paper is <i><a href="/wiki/The_San_Diego_Union-Tribune" title="The San Diego Union-Tribune">The San Diego Union-Tribune</a></i>, also known as <i>U-T San Diego</i>, is ranked 23rd in the country (by daily circulation) as of March 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[76]</a></sup> The <i>Union-Tribune</i> serves both San Diego County and neighboring <a href="/wiki/Imperial_County,_California" title="Imperial County, California">Imperial County</a>. The former <i><a href="/wiki/North_County_Times" title="North County Times">North County Times</a></i>, based in Escondido and serving portions of Riverside County and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_North_County,_California" title="San Diego North County, California">North County</a>, was purchased by the Union-Tribune in 2012 and closed down. For about a year after absorbing the North County Times the Union-Tribune published a North County edition,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[77]</a></sup> but the regional edition was later abandoned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horn_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Horn-82">[78]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> is also delivered in portions of the county. Many of the area's cities, towns and neighborhoods have their own local newspapers; the <i>Union Tribune</i> bought eight local weeklies in 2013 and is continuing to publish them as independent local newspapers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horn_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Horn-82">[78]</a></sup> The <i>San Diego Daily Transcript</i> reports business and legal news. Privately published papers like the <i>Military Press Newspaper</i> and the <i>Navy Dispatch</i> serve the military community both on and off base.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_media">Other media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Other media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=County_Television_Network&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="County Television Network (page does not exist)">County Television Network</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Public-access_television" title="Public-access television">public-access television</a> cable channel, offering a "hometown blend of <a href="/wiki/C-SPAN" title="C-SPAN">C-SPAN</a>, the Lifetime, History, Travel, and Discovery channels" for the county, and funded by fees paid by cable companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[79]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Port_of_San_Diego">The Port of San Diego</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Diego_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: The Port of San Diego">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Embarcadero_(San_Diego)" title="Embarcadero (San Diego)">Embarcadero (San Diego)</a></li>
